## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: materials science / constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material, a core problem in solid mechanics and materials science. Stress typically increases nonlinearly with strain (hardening) and decreases with temperature (thermal softening), with various constitutive models capturing these effects.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 + c2 * T) (linear elastic with T-dependent modulus)
- Hollomon power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (power-law strain hardening at fixed T)
- Hollomon with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 + c3 * T) (power-law hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook model: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T) (combined hardening and thermal effects)
- Johnson-Cook with homologous temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T**c4) (power-law thermal softening)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Ludwik with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (hardening with Arrhenius-type thermal term)
- Voce saturation model: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) (saturating stress with exponential approach)
- Voce with temperature: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * exp(c2 * T) (saturation hardening with thermal softening)
- Arrhenius-type flow stress: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon**c2 (thermally activated deformation)
- Polynomial elastic-plastic: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * T (quadratic strain with linear T)
- Sinh-based Sellars-Tegart: sigma = c0 * asinh(c1 * epsilon**c2 * exp(c3 * T)) (hot deformation flow stress)
- Combined power-exponential: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) * (c3 + c4 * epsilon) (general multiplicative form)
- Linear thermal + nonlinear strain: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon**c3 (polynomial thermal modulus with hardening)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening in metals → multiplicative factor (1 - c*(T/Tm)**m) or exp(-c*T) reducing stress at higher temperatures
- Strain hardening saturation → (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) form indicating stress approaching a plateau at large strains
- Power-law strain hardening → epsilon**n with 0 < n < 1 typical for metals (n is strain hardening exponent)
- Additive yield stress → constant c0 term added to strain-dependent terms representing initial yield before hardening
- Arrhenius thermal activation → exp(c*T) or exp(c/T) terms reflecting thermally activated dislocation mechanisms
- Multiplicative separability → sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T) when strain hardening and thermal softening act independently
- Inverse hyperbolic sine flow stress → asinh() form from Garofalo/Sellars-Tegart equation for creep/hot working
- Polynomial modulus degradation → E(T) = c0 + c1*T + c2*T**2 capturing gradual stiffness loss with temperature
